Zhang Jinghui Goes to the Capital to Assume Post as President of the Military Council 78

To Return to Harbin to Concurrently Hold Post After Taking Office

Harbin Correspondence - Zhang Jinghui, the Chief Executive of the Eastern Provinces Special Region, was appointed President of the Military Council by the Central Government. The official order was issued two months ago, but Zhang only departed southward on the evening of April 30th. He will not stop along the way and is scheduled to arrive in the capital before the opening of the National Assembly to first take office as President of the Military Council, so that he can participate in the ceremonies when the National Assembly convenes. He is scheduled to stay in the capital for one month and return to Harbin around early June. Thereafter, he will concurrently hold the post of President remotely. The reason why Zhang was not in a hurry to go to the capital was that the position of Chief Executive of the Eastern Provinces Special Region was also extremely important, and he was unwilling to travel far. Until recently, the Northeast authorities indicated that even though Zhang was going to the capital to take office, he could return to Harbin to lead remotely after staying for a while. Zhang then decided to depart southward. The affairs of the Chief Executive's Office will be temporarily handled by Bao Lian, the Director of the Department of Political Affairs. In case of important events, he will telegraph the capital for instructions. It is also heard that the Northeast authorities will discuss with the Central Government the system of the Eastern Provinces Special Region. If the provinces are reduced in size and the Special Region is changed into a province, or if it is completely abolished, Zhang Jinghui will also participate in this discussion after arriving in the capital. Therefore, this trip of Zhang's is of considerable importance. (May 1)

Hunan Disaster Victims to Implement Migration to the Northeast 79

The First Batch Temporarily Set at 500 People

Changsha Correspondence - Hunan Province is densely populated and has frequent disasters, resulting in unemployment for the four classes of people. The refugees from Pingjiang and Liuyang who are now in the provincial capital and unable to return home still number in the tens of thousands. Although all sectors are trying their best to raise funds for relief, it is difficult to reach everyone. The Hunan authorities believe that passive giving is ultimately unsustainable, so they have decided to migrate people to the Northeast as a positive remedy. They sent Cao Jihui to the Northeast for an on-the-ground investigation. He believes that Hunan Camp in Yilan County, Jilin Province, is sparsely populated, with an average of less than one person per square mile. If the surplus population of Hunan is used to fill the sparse population of the Northeast, the Eastern Provinces will not only reap the benefits of consolidating the borders, but Hunan Province will also alleviate the problem of overpopulation, and it can also develop land resources and expand people's livelihoods. Commissioner Cao returned to Hunan yesterday and immediately submitted a report to the provincial government, which decided to designate the Hunan Camp reclamation area in Yilan County, Jilin as the Hunan immigrant area. The first batch will temporarily move 500 people there, and the expenses are set at 50,000 yuan, which will be allocated from the relief funds. A migration office will be set up under the Hunan Provincial Relief Association, and Cao Jihui will be appointed as a commissioner to oversee the migration. A Hunan Migration Area Management Bureau will also be established in Hunan Camp in Yilan County, and Zhang Zuce will be appointed as a commissioner to handle matters related to the reception, registration, management, and protection of the settlers, the allocation of reclaimed land, and the autonomy of the reclaimed area. The first group of settlers is limited to arriving in the reclaimed area before the end of June, and preparations are currently underway. Yesterday, the Hunan Provincial Relief Association's Migration Office issued a notice to make all the key points of the migration widely known. (May 3)

Hebei Province to Levy Business Tax 80

To Offset Losses After Abolishing Likin

Tianjin Correspondence - Before the abolition of likin, the financial revenue of Hebei Province was about 24 million yuan per year. In addition to providing more than 10 million yuan for government expenses, the remainder was allocated to military expenses. However, after the implementation of likin abolition this year, revenue has been reduced by about 8 to 9 million yuan. The military and government expenses have caused great panic. Fortunately, the provincial treasury still had some surplus at the end of last year. Government expenses were issued at 80%, which could barely support for a few months. By the end of last month, the situation was already desperate. Therefore, starting from the first of this month, orders have been given to all departments to implement staff reductions and salary cuts. Recently, departments such as education, agriculture and mining, civil affairs, finance, and construction have cut one-third to one-half of their personnel in order to save money. The monthly expenses of each department have been reduced from about 14,000 to 15,000 yuan to 6,000 to 7,000 yuan. The provincial and municipal authorities had earlier proposed to quickly implement a business tax to offset the losses after the abolition of likin. During the time when Zang Qifang was acting mayor of Tianjin, discussions were held on whether the province and city should handle it separately, but no agreement was reached. Later, Zang left and Zhang Xueming was promoted to mayor. Wang Shuchang, the chairman of the province, spent more than a month in Shenyang discussing the financial problems of the province. If the business tax were handled separately by the province and city, then the commerce of Hebei would be concentrated in Tianjin, and the tax revenue in other places would be very small. Only by merging the province and city could the provincial treasury be supplemented. After repeated discussions with Deputy Commander Zhang, it was finally decided that the province and city would jointly handle it. After Wang returned to Tianjin, he ordered Yao Hong, the Director of the Department of Finance, to actively proceed. First, a Business Tax Preparatory Committee was established, and seven people were appointed as members: Yao Hong, Director of the Department of Finance, Zhang Xueming, Mayor, He Yufang, Director of the Department of Industry, Zhang Guochen, Director of the Bureau of Finance, Zhou Zhensheng, Secretary of the Municipal Government, Zhang Pintiming, Chairman of the Chamber of Commerce, and Liu Diou, a financial expert. The collection regulations were passed by the preparatory meeting yesterday and submitted to the Central Government for record. It is heard that the date of implementation is set to begin on June 1. (May 2)

The Tripitaka Sutra of Yexian County is Transported to Jinan for Preservation 81

The Previous Rumor of Burning Was Not Accurate

But A Portion Was Damaged

Jinan Correspondence - The Tripitaka Sutra of Hainan Temple in Yexian County, Shandong Province, was originally known as the complete copy in the country. In recent years, it has been lost due to repeated moves. A rumor has circulated a month ago that the sutra was burned by the Normal School lecture hall. The Education Department, therefore, specially sent Wang Xiantang, the director of the Provincial Library, to Yexian to investigate the truth. He learned that the rumor of burning was not accurate, but the loss was very severe. If it is not transported to Jinan for proper preservation, the famous and precious books will eventually be completely damaged. Therefore, 2,275 volumes of the complete ones, packed in eight boxes, and the broken ones, packed in eighteen burlap bags, were transported to the Jinan Library on April 23. Because they wanted to make it a complete set with the old ones, they are currently organizing the old shelves and compiling the catalog every day. The report submitted by Wang Xiantang to the Education Department is recorded below: "In the case of the order No. 1288 from your department, the Tripitaka Sutra of Hainan Temple in Yexian County was damaged, and I was ordered to cooperate with the county magistrate and the county supervisor of education to find a way to transport and preserve it. After receiving this order, I arrived in Yexian County on the 11th of this month and went to Hainan Temple with County Magistrate Ma Zhenfan and Supervisor Peng Rulin to investigate and discuss the transportation. County Magistrate Ma convened a meeting of all sectors and unanimously agreed to hand it over to Xiantang for preservation in the library. This Tripitaka Sutra is a Ming Dynasty version of the Sanskrit Sutra. During the Shunzhi period of the early Qing Dynasty, Zhang Duan, a scholar from Yexian, converted his family temple into Qingchan Temple, also known as Dabei Pavilion, in the northeast corner of the city. He purchased the entire Tripitaka Sutra and donated it to the temple. Last year, the army occupied the temple and did not know how to protect it, so it was arbitrarily damaged. Huang Da, the former county magistrate of Yexian, ordered people to sort out the debris and transport it to the current Hainan Temple building. Later, Hainan Temple was borrowed by the militia group. After the militia group left, in March of this year, the county magistrate ordered the Normal School lecture hall to move to Hainan Temple because there were no suitable rooms. At that time, the remaining Tripitaka Sutra had been moved from the upstairs and was in a mess. According to the Director of the County Education Bureau and the Director of the Normal School lecture hall, the sutras were scattered downstairs at that time, and the students were supervised to sort them out separately. Some of the complete ones were stored upstairs and hidden with boards. The rest of the broken and incomplete ones could not be sorted out and were piled in the bell tower of the temple. The four sides were also made of boards to cover them. The county decided to transport the sutra, so Xiantang immediately purchased wooden boxes and burlap bags the next day and went to the temple to open the panels and count them with the staff, teachers, and students. There were 2,275 complete volumes, all packed in boxes. The rest was all scrap paper that could not be counted, totaling eight large wooden boxes and eighteen burlap bags. He immediately compiled the numbers, affixed seals, and obtained a passport from the county government. On the 13th, he used a large cart to transport them to Weixian and handed them over to Yuelai Transportation Company. They were transported to Jinan and arrived at the library on the 23rd of this month. In addition to sorting them out and putting them on the shelves, I am also compiling a catalog. I should report the details of the handling process in detail for your review and record." (May 4)

Haiyuan Pavilion 82

The Loss of Books and Its Aftermath 83

Wang Xiantang's Findings

Jinan Correspondence - In the past year, the problem of the Haiyuan Pavilion library of the Yang family in Liaocheng has attracted the attention of the people of the country. The Ministry of Interior and the Ministry of Education have repeatedly sent letters to the Shandong Provincial Government to transfer orders to the Department of Civil Affairs and the Department of Education to investigate the matter. However, Wang Xiantang, the director of the Shandong Provincial Library, has also been involved in this matter from beginning to end. Due to his responsibilities, he has been thinking about including the treasures and secrets of the Haiyuan Pavilion into the library for proper preservation, so that it can be immortalized along with the Magpie Mountain and the Ming Lake. Therefore, he has put a lot of effort into collecting the books of the Haiyuan Pavilion. In the winter of the 18th year of the Republic, Wang was ordered to go to Liaocheng Haiyuan Pavilion to conduct an on-the-spot investigation. After returning, he wrote a book called "The Past and Present of the Haiyuan Pavilion Library of the Yang Family in Liaocheng" for the public to review. Since then, booksellers in Pingjin and Jinan have been running back and forth to Liaocheng and Jinan to buy the books of the Haiyuan Pavilion. Because Wang is good at appraising bronzes, stone carvings, calligraphy and painting, and versions of books, he must have Wang review them whenever he gets something. Therefore, Wang, although he did not buy the books sold by the Haiyuan Pavilion, he has seen most of them. Recently, Wang wrote another article entitled "The Loss of Books and the Aftermath of the Haiyuan Pavilion Library" based on his years of experience. It describes in detail the number and value of the books lost in the Haiyuan Pavilion. Before the article is published, it is first recorded here to awaken the attention of the people of the country. The article is as follows:

"The Haiyuan Pavilion Library of the Yang family in Liaocheng has suffered repeated banditry in recent years. The previous losses have been briefly described in the previous booklet, "The Past and Present of the Haiyuan Pavilion Library of the Yang Family in Liaocheng." The reports at that time were all based on actual surveys, and the facts were up to the time the survey was completed. In the year since the publication of this booklet, the Yang family's collection of books has continued to suffer from banditry and losses have increased. Now, based on the results of the investigation, I will describe them in detail below. After I returned to Jinan from the survey, the government authorities once made a resolution on the aftercare measures and were in the process of handling it. Bandits rose up near the area and the roads were blocked. Then, the bandits occupied Liaocheng and set up camp in the Haiyuan Pavilion. After the bandits left, there were troops who were recruited and reorganized into the city. This came and went continuously, and it was impossible to describe their names in detail. However, it is known that Wang Guanjun was the one who seized the most books. After the bandits occupied Liaocheng, the government could not negotiate with the Yang family about the library. Then, the war broke out in various places and the political situation changed. The provincial government moved to Qingdao and was in a state of turmoil, so there was no time to deal with this matter. When the overall situation was settled and the provincial government moved to Jinan, the bandits in the area were also gradually suppressed, but the secret books and rare books of the Haiyuan Pavilion had been swept away. The best of the Yang family's rare books were transported to Tianjin earlier. The losses this time were all the books recorded in my booklet and ordinary Ming and Qing versions. When the bandits occupied Liaocheng, they often sold the Yang family's books. The buyers gave prices at will, without paying much attention to them. Sometimes they were cut up to wrap things, cook food, or taken out as pillows. But this was still less than 1% of the collection because the Yang family had too many books. When Wang Guanjun entered the city with his newly recruited troops, he knew that the Yang family's collection of books was beautiful, rich, and valuable, so he invited a book and antique expert from Tianjin, known as Ninth Master, to Liaocheng to thoroughly inspect the rare books and all valuable books, inscriptions, calligraphy, and paintings. At the same time, in the name of harboring bandits, he thoroughly searched the residents inside and outside the city. All private books, calligraphy, and antiques were also swept away. It is also heard that the eight volumes of the Song edition Xianchun Lin'an Zhi of the Yang family were taken into a civilian's house by bandits to be used as a pillow. Wang's army searched for it, fearing that they would be implicated, so they burned the Lin'an Zhi and chopped up the book box for cooking. When I went to investigate, I only saw two volumes of Lin'an Zhi. The book box still existed. It is quite incomprehensible that four more volumes have suddenly been added this time. In short, the Haiyuan Pavilion Library suffered the only major catastrophe in the past this time. (To be continued)

The Disaster Relief Committee for the five counties of Huangchuan, Guangshan, Gushi, Luoshan, and Shangcheng in Henan has announced its establishment. He signed a contract with Shi Jiu'ao, the representative of the bank, stipulating that the loan would be for a term of three years from April 30, with a monthly interest rate of 7%. Small Steamer and Cargo Ship Robbed at the Same Time - The Herong small steamer of the Tongli Shipping Company, which runs daily between Dangkou Town, which borders Suzhou and Wuxi, and Baqian in Kunshan, was carrying more than 30 passengers at 4:00 PM on the 4th when it suddenly encountered five bandit ships in Xinkai River Township, which borders Kunshan and Changshu. The bandit ships surrounded the steamer, and more than ten bandits on board, all speaking the Chaohu dialect, took out box cannons and fired at the steamer. The glass windows and cabin doors of the steamer were destroyed. The deputy captain, Tao Ada, and Tao Zi were both slightly injured by stray bullets. The steamer stopped and let the bandits board and rob them. The bandits robbed passengers of silver, clothes, and other items worth about 500 yuan. At the same time, a cargo ship of the Shanghai Laogongmao Shipping Company, which was heading to Wuxi, also passed by and was robbed, suffering greater losses. The bandit ships then fled towards Yangcheng Lake. When the bandits were robbing, Pang Diancai, the county magistrate of Kunshan, was returning to his hometown in Changshu for something. When the ship passed by the place and heard gunfire in front, he returned to Dongtangshi in Changshu to report to the third squad of the 13th water police team, which in turn reported to the 13th team headquarters. That night, the team leader, Yang Qingjiu, led the team to pursue the bandits. When they arrived at the Xiaojing Yang Santai Temple area of Yangcheng Lake, they searched but did not find the bandits. They returned to Changshu on the 6th. The Herong small steamer is currently still docked at Xiaohengjing.

The Main Culprit in the Murder Case Was Apprehended - Lu Deguan, a bookkeeper from the family of Liu Kuangfeng, a villager in Liujiaqiao Township, District 8, went to Yin Zenrong's place in Yinxiang Lane on August 13 of the 17th year of the Republic to search for a thousand marks due to a dispute over land. A Kidnapping Case Occurred in Huaishang City - Chen Fengyi, 64 years old, and his wife, Yan, 61 years old, residents of Guanwuqiao Tulili in the 463th area, 7th district (Huaishang City), were from a well-to-do family, but were sterile and adopted Sun Honggen, the son of Sun Mou from Sun Lane, Hexi, Bashiqiao, Tianshang City, as their stepson 20 years ago, and also adopted a stepdaughter named Dajie, while Honggen has been idle and wandering, specializing in associating with idlers in recent years. The Condition of Mulberry, Soybean, and Wheat in the Four Rural Areas - The silkworms came out late this spring. The native species have been sleeping for the second time, and the foreign species have started to pupate. Some have just come out. There has been a lot of rain recently, and it is not suitable for the silkworms to eat wet leaves. Because the market price was very low last year, the market price this year is also depressed, about one yuan per dan, and no one is interested. Due to continuous rain and snow last winter and heavy spring snow this spring, plowing and fertilization were delayed. In mid-April, there were several days of heavy frost, which caused the ears of wheat to turn white during fruiting, reducing the harvest. The mulberry buds were also damaged. This was unexpected by the farmers. Two days of heavy rain caused the river water to rise by a foot, and the low-lying soybean and wheat fields were submerged in water, further jeopardizing the prospects for harvesting.

Garrison Headquarters 95

Crackdown on a Pseudo-Military Organization 96

Xu Fubo Arrested

On the 5th of this month, Deng Jingming, the head of the Investigation Team of the Garrison Headquarters, received a tip that a pseudo-military organization was operating in areas such as Beile Road in the French Concession. Deng had already heard rumors about this a few days prior. After dispatching officers for a secret investigation, it was confirmed that the information was credible, and it matched the tip received on that day. Without alarming the suspects, Deng dispatched investigators Yang Fengqi, Xu Pengfei, Wang Bin, Yao Ding, and others, together with Chinese and foreign detectives from the French Concession Police, to raid No. 19 Laotianxiang Lane, Beile Road, at 2:00 AM. They successfully dismantled a pseudo-Naval Defense Guerrilla Headquarters. The team apprehended Zheng Duo, a pseudo-captain; Yin Zhanyuan, an adjutant; Xie Heqing, a quartermaster; Ma Zhibing, a special agent; Shao Lisheng, a cook; and Xie Atang, the sixth person. Two suitcases and a wicker basket of incriminating evidence were seized, including a pseudo-carved wooden seal, uniforms, armed belts, letters of appointment, and official documents. Xu Fubo, a pseudo-commander, was arrested at the Datong Apartment on Malang Road, and Shu Bin, a pseudo-chief of staff, was arrested at Jingyi Lane on the same road. The suspects and the evidence were temporarily detained at the French Concession Police Station. It is reported that the team has submitted a request to the Garrison Headquarters to transfer the suspects for interrogation. According to investigations, Xu Fubo and others, relying on their false title of commander, issued appointments indiscriminately, sold official positions, and swindled money from gullible individuals seeking official positions. It is said that a certain Mr. Li was defrauded of several thousand gold pieces in exchange for a worthless letter of appointment. (New Sound News Agency Reporter's Note: This article was submitted by the Investigation Team of the Garrison Headquarters for publication in our agency.)

Industrial Survey Begins 104

Divided into Eight Districts

To be Completed in Three Months

The Shanghai Industrial Survey Joint Office, organized by the Bureau of Statistics of the Legislative Yuan, the Ministry of Industry, the Shanghai Social Affairs Bureau, the China Economic Society, and the Research Institute of Jiaotong University, began surveying factories yesterday. A Daily News reporter interviewed Zhang Zongbi, a staff member of the office, who stated that the survey team consists of eight individuals: Qian Shouzhi, Qin Wanzhi, Lin Mingqi, Shi Haoran, Cao Dianhao, Zheng He, Gao Jiadong, and Jin Yufan. Zhang and Tian Heqing will be responsible for reviewing the survey forms. Jiaotong University's Research Institute has the most members assigned, followed by the Social Affairs Bureau. The area is roughly divided into eight districts, from Wusong in the east to Zoupura in the west, and the survey only covers machine factories and manual factories owned by Chinese. Reports will be submitted regularly, with a deadline of three months for completion. If the number of factories is too large to complete within the deadline, an extension may be granted. The survey will cover twenty items: (1) Factory name, (2) Address (main factory, branch factory, distribution office), (3) Name of factory owner or manager, (4) Type of industry, (5) Year of establishment or reorganization, (6) Factory name before reorganization, (7) Capital organization (sole proprietorship, partnership, limited liability, unlimited liability, etc.), (8) Capital amount, whether there are foreign shares, amount of public reserve, (9) Number of staff and salaries, (10) Number of workers and wages, (11) Working hours, (12) Whether there is night work, (13) Whether the factory provides meals, (14) Whether the factory provides accommodation, (15) Factory building type, (16) Power source of machinery in the factory, (17) Processing machine, (18) Raw materials, (19) Products, (20) Remarks.

Joint Federation Seeks to Resolve Coal Transport Issues 105

Sends Qian Chengxu to Tianjin for Investigation

Domestic factories rely heavily on Kailuan coal. Recently, a dispute suddenly arose between Kailuan Mines and the Beining Railway Bureau, causing a shortage of coal on the market, which has affected industrial production and the livelihood of workers. The impact is not limited to the influx of Japanese coal into China. The China Industrial Federation has received numerous letters and telegrams from members in various regions requesting negotiations with the Kailuan Shanghai office. The office and users are also facing legal responsibility due to the lack of coal to distribute. The dispute has lasted for over a month without a resolution. Factories are losing approximately $100,000 per day. The cause of the dispute between Kailuan Mines and the Beining Railway Bureau remains a secret, and the true situation remains unclear to the outside world. Recently, the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce and the China Industrial Federation have negotiated, believing that the continued dispute is detrimental to both industry and commerce. As Dr. Qian Chengxu was invited to Tianjin and Beijing to lecture on China's industrial construction, he was publicly recommended to resolve the coal transportation issues. Qian will travel from Shanghai to Nanjing on the 7th to discuss the matter with the government and is expected to depart for Beijing around the 10th.

Kailuan Coal Dispute Resolved 106

Agreement Reached Yesterday 107

25% to be Supplied Before End of June

Remaining Coal Supplied Equally Within the Year

Both Parties Agree to Sign the Contract Yesterday

Yuan Tai and Quan Tai, the Shanghai distribution offices of Kailuan Coal Mine, previously experienced a disruption in the supply of Kailuan coal, resulting in over 100,000 tons of coal owed to 16 coal companies, including Xinyi Company, leading to losses and disputes. The Social Affairs Bureau convened both parties for mediation, and preliminary terms were set, with both parties agreeing to resolve the matter privately. Yesterday at 2:00 PM, the Shanghai Coal Trade Association reconvened Yuan Tai, Quan Tai, and the 16 coal companies, including Xinyi Company, for a mediation meeting. The meeting was chaired by Mao Chunpu, and a settlement was reached at 5:00 PM. Both parties signed a contract. The original text of the contract is recorded below.

Mediation Document of the Shanghai Coal Trade Association

Parties Involved: Coal Companies Xinyi Company and 15 others; Respondents: Coal Companies Yuan Tai Company and Quan Tai Coal Company; Case: Failure to deliver Kailuan coal according to the agreed quantities, resulting in losses due to the substitution of higher-priced coal, Dispute Mediation Result: (1) From May 5th to the end of June, at least 25% of the contracted coal will be delivered. Additional deliveries will be made as possible. From July 1st, the remaining coal from January, February, March, April, May, and June will be delivered equally on a monthly basis until December 15th of this year, with any outstanding amounts to be cleared in full. Contracts expiring in any month will be extended to December 15th. (2) Coal from this invoice must be delivered in full within May and June. Any shortages will be compensated with coal of equal value. Both parties are exempt from storage and interest charges. The above mediation result is verified to be consistent with the original draft.

Signatories:

Mediation Director: Mao Chunpu

Issuer: Yuan Tai Company, Zhang Zhangkui; Quan Tai Coal Company, Hu Changfa

Contracting Parties: Xinyi Company, Luo Deyou; Tongyu, Li Ganghong; Senmao, Bao Zhexun; Junchang, Huang Jieren; Dalongxing, Luo Huaibing; Shengshun, Luo ChunKui; Renhe, Lin Lusheng; Laoyongchang, Pan Yisan; Yuancheng, Wu Shijie; Fuda, Yao Qilin; Hongchang, Xia Zonghai; Ruida, Wu Weijun; Yuansheng, Chen Keren; Yuancheng, Wang Shaocheng; Yicheng, Jiang Runxin.

New Construction in the Shipping Industry 110

Shipping Association Reorganized

The Shanghai Shipping Association, an organization of over seventy shipping companies, handles disputes within the shipping industry and deals with business-related conflicts. It has been quite effective since its establishment. The Ministry of Communications has revised the regulations for the organization of shipping associations and issued them to Shanghai yesterday, ordering the association to reorganize according to the new regulations. The association has followed this order and set up a preparatory office on the third floor of No. 10 Guangdong Road. The new articles of association stipulate that the shipping association regulations promulgated on December 14, 16, have been repealed, and the association will be reorganized in accordance with the regulations for industrial and commercial associations and people's organizations. Membership of the shipping association is stipulated to be (1) those engaged in shipping and transportation, (2) those engaged in commercial vessel leasing, and (3) those engaged in commercial shipbuilding. If there are seven or more branch offices in one location, an association may be formed, but no more than two associations may be established in the same location. The tasks of the association are also clearly defined as (1) researching improvements in shipping, (2) protecting the interests of the shipping industry, (3) mediating disputes and arbitration in the shipping industry, (4) forwarding official documents and reports relating to shipping, (5) preparing statistics, etc. After receiving this order yesterday, the Shanghai Shipping Association dissolved the original association and reorganized it as a preparatory office in accordance with the new articles of association.

Quickly Establish Marine Insurance

The Shanghai shipping industry is planning to establish a marine insurance company. In late March, the eight major shipping companies in the city agreed to establish the company, but it has not yet been established due to unpaid shares. Now, ship accidents are occurring frequently, and disputes are arising over the loss and compensation of sailors. The initiators have held subsequent meetings, calling for the urgent establishment of the company. Yesterday, a special notice was issued to all shipping companies stating that the original proposal to establish marine insurance was to provide shipowners with a means of self-help and to protect sailors from unexpected dangers. Although the initiators identified the shares on March 28, the company has not yet been established. Given the recent accidents involving the Dachang and Daji ships, the urgency of this insurance is even more apparent. Yesterday, the original initiators held a meeting to discuss the matter, and the following measures were decided: The identified shares should be paid from May 15th to 31st. Yu Qiaqing was appointed as the head of the preparatory committee, and Chen Ganqing and Shen Zhongyi were appointed as members of the preparatory committee. The shares should be deposited with the Ningbo Commercial Bank for collection to facilitate early establishment.

Business Representative Attending the National Assembly 112

Wang Yansong Petitions Legislative Yuan 113

To Exempt Export Taxes on Silk, Chinese Tea, Embroidery, etc.

To Clearly Define Exemption Scope in Business Tax Law

Requests Early Enactment of Money Shop Law to Benefit Commerce

Wang Yansong, the representative of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce and industrial organizations to the National Assembly, took a special train to Nanjing on the 3rd and stayed at the Central Hotel. In addition to reporting to the National Assembly Office the day before yesterday, Wang also went to the Legislative Yuan in the afternoon to present detailed arguments regarding the requests to exempt export taxes on silk, Chinese tea, embroidery, etc., to clearly define exemption standards when enacting the business tax law, and to enact the Money Shop Law. It is reported that the members of the Legislative Yuan expressed their willingness to accommodate these requests as much as possible. The following is the original text of Wang's submission:

Respectfully submitted: I, Yansong, am a representative to the National Assembly elected by the Shanghai business community. Before my departure, I was entrusted by 180 trade associations in the city to alleviate the suffering of merchants and people. How could I dare to remain silent about the ardent hopes of the merchants and the weight of my responsibilities? Now, I humbly present the points of request from the Shanghai merchants and people to the Legislative Yuan: (1) Please exempt export taxes on silk, Chinese tea, embroidery, etc. I heard that the export tax law is still under consideration by the Legislative Yuan. It was previously reported that the Ministry of Finance plans to abolish the regular customs duties within fifty li after increasing export taxes, while the regular customs duties collect about 6 million yuan annually. According to the Ministry of Finance's original proposal for the new export tax law, it can increase revenue to 20 million yuan annually. Even according to the Legislative Yuan's initial review, it can collect up to 16 million yuan, which is higher than the old tax law. However, our country is a country with a trade deficit, and foreign trade has long suffered from depression. The government has the responsibility to encourage and promote it. Silk and Chinese tea, which are the most important exports of our country, have also had their overseas sales taken away by others. In addition, the tariff barriers of various countries are heavily levied, which may lead to prohibition. I earnestly request that the Legislative Yuan, when reviewing the new tax law this time, exempt all export taxes on silk, Chinese tea, embroidery, etc., which should be expanded in overseas sales, to show protection. (2) Please clearly define the exemption standards in the business tax law. The business tax law has been approved by the Legislative Yuan, and members Chen Changheng and Shi Weihuan are drafting it. How can we relieve the suffering of merchants and people and avoid repeating the mistakes of likin? The members of the committee have given deep consideration and mature thought to this issue. However, the business tax is a universal tax. If we are not careful, its harassment will be even worse than likin. The opinions of various industries on the business tax have been submitted by the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce and various industry associations in letters and telegrams at any time. The main points are: (1) In accordance with the resolution on abolishing likin, the tax rate should not exceed two per thousand. (2) The scope of luxury businesses and businesses that should be banned from taxation should be clearly defined. We should also confirm that luxury businesses are not the same as luxury goods. (3) Agents who do not directly sell goods should be exempt from tax. (4)

Page 10

Please continue to exempt business tax on goods that were originally exempt from likin, such as native cloth. (5) Businesses engaged in foreign trade should be exempted from tax or have their taxes reduced. (6) Determine the principle of one tax per item. No taxes or levies may be collected in any name other than the business tax. (7) In accordance with the resolution of the Central Political Council, provinces may not start collecting taxes before the Legislative Yuan has reviewed and approved them. If there are any increases in tax rates in the future, they should also be approved by the Legislative Yuan before they can be implemented. I earnestly request that the above seven items be clearly stipulated in the business tax law for compliance. (3) Please enact the Money Shop Law to benefit commerce. The banking and money industries are both the hub of all industries in our country. Banks mainly provide loans with mortgages, but in terms of the current commercial relationship, the money industry is even more common and important. If we must force money shops to use banking laws, then it will inevitably affect commerce. The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce and the Shanghai Money Industry Association have telegraphed in detail the reasons for this. Please adopt them and enact them as soon as possible.

Shanghai Municipal General Chamber of Commerce 114

Requests Maintenance of Original Special Tax 115

Exempts Customs Duty on Foil Products

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce believes that the imposition of both special business tax and customs duty on foil products contradicts the principle that special taxes, once paid in full, should be valid throughout the country. Yesterday, the chamber telegraphed the Ministry of Finance again, requesting the maintenance of the original special tax and exemption from further customs duty on foil products. The original telegram stated: "To the Ministry of Finance in Nanjing: This association is requesting the correction of the overlapping taxation of special business tax on foil products. On April 30th, we received your Ministry's telegram in response, stating that the business tax is levied on the act of business and not on goods. Regardless of whether any goods have paid the business tax or not, they must pay customs duty in accordance with the regulations when transported through customs. The case of foil products is the same. The request for exemption is difficult to approve, etc. The association has reviewed the telegram sent on the 15th, which is divided into three points. The first point is that although the original text of the Zhejiang Department of Finance's report states that it still follows the old rules, extracting twelve and a half percent, the new rules extract fifteen percent, which is inconsistent with the old rules. The second point is that after the special tax is paid in full, it is valid throughout the country, while this time it is limited to the provinces of Jiangsu and Zhejiang, which is also inconsistent with the old rules. The current approval from your Ministry does not mention these two points, and we request that the original case be investigated and corrected. The third point is that the current approval states that the business tax is levied on the act of business and not on goods. Regardless of whether any goods have paid the business tax or not, they must pay customs duty in accordance with the regulations when transported through customs, etc. The association believes that the special business tax on foil products implemented in Zhejiang Province is a disguised special tax that is not consistent with the principles of business tax. For example, the tax rate is levied as a percentage instead of per thousand, and the tax amount is not directly paid by the taxpayer to the competent authority, but is contracted out to others. All of these are in violation of the outline and supplementary measures. The main point is that the business tax is levied on the act of business and not on goods, while the special business tax on foil products currently collected in Zhejiang Province is levied once for each batch of goods sold. It is also found that the tax schedule is based on the thickness of the goods. There are five checkpoints along the route from Shaoxing to Shanghai. How can this be said to not be a tax on goods? The provincial government is trying to excuse itself with sophistry. Since all the taxation methods in the province are based on the old special tax regulations, the old rule that customs duty is no longer paid once the tax has been paid should be fully applied. Otherwise, other industries will have their burdens reduced by abolishing likin, while this industry alone will have its tax burden increased by abolishing likin. This is unfair in terms of government orders. Based on the above reasons, we are sending another telegram to your ministry to ask for your review and approval to maintain the original special tax on foil products and to exempt them from further customs duty to alleviate the difficulties of merchants and facilitate public convenience. The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce respectfully."

Shanghai Municipal General Chamber of Commerce 116

Interprets Scope of Brokerage Tax 117

No Additional Business Tax on Those Who Have Paid Brokerage Tax

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to the Tea Trade Association yesterday, stating: "We received your letter on April 28th, asking for an explanation on whether the brokerage tax is within the scope of special taxes, and stating that tea businesses have meager profits and cannot be taxed at two per thousand like shops, but can only be taxed at five jiao per thousand yuan. The answers are as follows: (1) The brokerage tax has long been used as provincial revenue and is managed by the Provincial Education Fund Management Office. It is not within the scope of central special taxes. (2) Tea businesses that have paid brokerage tax are different from tea shops. In accordance with Article 11 of the Supplementary Measures to the Business Tax promulgated by the Ministry, the brokerage tax will be renamed the business tax in the current first transitional step, and the tax rate will remain the same as the original brokerage tax."

Trademark Bureau 118

Crackdown on Counterfeit National Product Trademarks 119

Attached is the original opinion

The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau yesterday issued a directive to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, stating that it was ordered to comply with the matter. The Ministry of Industry's directive, Industry Character No. 2934, stated that the members of the Industry and Commerce Conference, Chen Yaoyuan, etc., proposed that tax-free ports should be banned from altering the decoration and trademarks of foreign products to pass them off as local products and sell them in the mainland to evade export taxes and maintain the local manufacturing industry. After the conference passed the resolution, the Ministry believed that unscrupulous merchants impersonating national product trademarks should be banned according to law. However, the case did not state the facts clearly, so it was impossible to stop it. The Trademark Bureau was ordered to submit its opinions for verification. Now, the Trademark Bureau's report and attached opinion were received by the Ministry. The letter is divided into three categories, totaling ten items. The third item of the second category and the second and third items of the third category are all related to various commercial organizations. It is found that unscrupulous merchants are cunning and have many tricks. It is difficult for those who are not familiar with the local situation to know where they are hiding. It is appropriate to copy and distribute the original opinion letter to let them know that if unscrupulous elements are used by foreign merchants, they are allowed to submit evidence and request investigation to prevent impersonation. This order, etc. A copy of the original opinion letter is attached. Upon receiving this, the original opinion letter shall be copied and distributed to the association to instruct all trade associations to comply with this order. Now, the original opinion letter is attached as follows: (A) Cases of discovering foreign goods impersonating national product trademarks that have been rejected: (1) The Butterfly China Positive Trademark and its joint trademark of the Japanese Asahi Match Co., Ltd. were ordered to be changed to the Guohua trademark because the submitted design had prominent Chinese characters before being reviewed and approved separately. (2) The Laifu trademark of the Japanese Nissin Match Co., Ltd. was rejected because there were two characters "Guohuo" (national product) in the upper corners of the design, and registration was not allowed. (B) Proposed opinions on cracking down on foreign goods impersonating national product trademarks: (1) When applying for registration of trademarks and designs with explicit expressions such as "Guohuo" (national product), "Guochan" (domestic product), "Zhonghua Zhizao" (Made in China), or implicit meanings of national products such as "Resist Foreign Goods and Recover Rights," the bureau should carefully examine them and strictly reject them. (2) When submitting commodity samples and decorations to the bureau for trademark cases, the bureau should pay attention to detailed inspection at any time. If it is found outside the decision that foreign goods are impersonating national products by using words or are suspected of impersonating, it should be reported to the Ministry to instruct the competent authorities to investigate and handle it. (3) Continue to print national product trademarks for identification, but the printing of national product trademarks is based on whether the applicant's nationality is Chinese. Whether the products used are purely domestic-made should be investigated separately by various business organizations and competent national product authorities. (4) If there is a foreign product counterfeiting a trademark and impersonating a national product, the circumstances are more serious than ordinary trademark counterfeiting and should be transferred to the court for strict punishment. (C) Views on cracking down on foreign goods impersonating national products: (1) It is advisable to start from the customs. When encountering local goods for transshipment, a detailed inspection must be carried out to avoid confusion. (2) Businessmen must know about large quantities of goods being transported to other ports. Local goods factories and trade associations should investigate at any time whether there are unscrupulous elements being used by foreign merchants. If they are indeed national products, they should be certified by the trade association. (3) Investigate the manufacturing capacity of each factory producing products. If the output exceeds its capacity, it is inevitable that foreign goods are being repackaged. Strict investigation and crackdown should be carried out. (4) Strictly stipulate the penalty for foreign goods impersonating national products.

In recent years, China has been under economic pressure from foreigners, resulting in backward production and declining markets. Chen Wenlin's Talk on Aviation in Fujian Province 121

Mr. Chen is scheduled to return to Fujian by boat today

Mr. Chen Wenlin, Director of the Xiamen Naval Aviation Training Center, returned to Shanghai after attending the aviation conference in Beijing and is currently staying at sea. Yesterday, a reporter from the Guowen News Agency met Mr. Chen at his residence and asked about the aviation situation in Fujian Province. According to him, Fujian Province has never had an aviation team. All existing teams were created by the Navy. There were originally three agencies: (1) the Naval Aviation Office, (2) the Mawei Naval Aircraft Manufacturing Office, and (3) the Naval Aviation Training Center, which I presided over. Later, the first two agencies moved to Shanghai one after another, so the only one currently in Fujian is the Training Center, which has about ten training aircraft under its jurisdiction. In addition to the daily training of students, during the campaign against Lu (Xingbang), Fujian Province lacked air force, so at that time, the aircraft of our department assisted the army to work on the front line for a time. But it has now been pacified. There are a small number of Red bandits harassing the western part of Fujian, so sometimes the aircraft of our department are also transferred to suppress them. Director Zhang (Huichang) met me in Beijing and he did have a slight illness, but I don't know which hospital he went to in Shanghai. This time, I attended the aviation conference, firstly as a representative of the Fujian Provincial Naval Aviation, and secondly because the conference asked me to serve as an expert. Therefore, I came to Beijing and now I need to report the process of the conference back to Fujian, so I have decided to take the boat tomorrow (today) at noon.

Fisheries Guidance Institute Established Yesterday 127

The Shanghai Municipal Fisheries Guidance Institute has been in preparation for a long time and was officially established yesterday (the 6th). A reporter from the Industry and Commerce Society visited Mr. Zhou Jianyin, the director of the institute, at the old site of the former Finance Ministry's Jiangsu-Zhejiang Fisheries Affairs Bureau in Taili Lane, Laoximen. When asked about the purpose of the establishment of the guidance institute, he replied that Shanghai is located in the Yangtze River Basin and a coastal hub. It is not only the hub of the fisheries of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, but also the only base for the new-style fisheries in the country. The position in the great fisheries is extremely important. Director Pan of the Social Affairs Bureau has always been determined to improve fisheries. Considering that the rise and fall of fisheries in this city is of great concern to the national economy and people's livelihood, he approved the Municipal Government to prepare to establish a fisheries guidance institute in August last year as a specialized agency to improve fisheries in this city. Later, due to funding issues, it could not be established for a time. In November, the Social Affairs Bureau, considering that foreign encroachment on fishing was becoming more and more serious and that domestic fisheries were becoming more and more depressed, continued to actively prepare for the establishment of the guidance institute on the one hand, and initiated the organization of the Fisheries Improvement Propaganda Association together with the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Agriculture and Mining. It held an expanded propaganda week at the Shanghai Civil Middle School last month. The details have been reported in various newspapers. At that time, I (Director Zhou said himself) was commissioned to prepare for the work, and Mr. Wang Defa was commissioned to serve as a technician to assist in everything. It was not until today that it was officially established. Everything is still in its infancy. I hope that the public opinion will provide assistance from time to time so that it can proceed smoothly and the result will be twice the result with half the effort.

Great Fortune Wheel Collision Case 128

Report from Ping An Company

Guomin News Agency stated that the Great Fortune Wheel of the Dahua Company collided with the Great Fortune Wheel of the Ping An Company outside Wusongkou, and the Great Fortune Wheel immediately sank. The situation has been reported in previous reports. It is now learned that the Ping An Company, the owner of the Great Fortune Wheel, sent a letter to the Shanghai Shipping Association, stating (excerpt above) that the Great Fortune Wheel of our company set sail from the third wharf in Hudong, Shanghai at 6:50 pm on April 14 to Dinghai, Shipu, Haimen and other ports. The night was dark and the sky was clear. Since the ship was driven by Captain Ge Ashi, it was 8:20 pm when the ship passed the Lisnore buoy. The captain then corrected the direction and proceeded along the downstream channel towards the Block House buoy. Then, the second mate and Jiangbei leader Bei Shifu drove the ship. The captain stayed by his side for a moment and saw no ships on the sea. He left the pilot house for about eight minutes. The second mate saw the masthead light and the green light on the side of a ship in front of him. The ship was coming from a position three characters off the starboard bow of the Great Fortune Wheel. The two ships did not shout back. At that time, the Great Fortune Wheel was in the downstream channel and was sailing according to the regulations. Although the Great Fortune Wheel was three characters off the starboard bow, its bow was not directly facing the Great Fortune Wheel. The two ships could pass each other without any risk of magnetic collision. Unexpectedly, the Great Fortune Wheel suddenly pulled four loud horn signals in a row. As soon as the captain of the Great Fortune Wheel heard the horn signal, he immediately went to the deck and entered the pilot house. He still saw the green light of the Great Fortune Wheel coming towards him. When the two ships were only a few ship lengths apart, the Great Fortune Wheel suddenly changed direction and passed over the bow of the Great Fortune Wheel to the right. The captain of the Great Fortune Wheel knew that something was wrong and immediately pulled the whistle three times and stopped the engine and opened the full speed reverse engine. But it still could not avoid the collision. Then, the middle of the port side of the Great Fortune Wheel collided with the bow of the Great Fortune Wheel. After the accident, the Great Fortune Wheel checked whether the ship was in danger of sinking. It was found that there was no major problem for the time being. It approached the Great Fortune Wheel to carry out rescue and transferred all the passengers and crew of the Great Fortune Wheel. After inquiring and confirming that no one was left on the ship, the Great Fortune Wheel began to drive back to Wusong and anchor. A customs fireboat came and the captain and second mate of the Great Fortune Wheel and the captain of the Great Fortune Wheel took the customs ship to the Wusong Customs to report the collision. It was found that the accident was entirely caused by the fault of the driver of the Great Fortune Wheel. The Great Fortune Wheel of our company suffered a great loss as a result. We have informed the Dahua Company to demand compensation. According to the company's reply, not only did they not admit liability for compensation, but they wanted our company to compensate them. The dispute between the two parties has not been resolved. Although the sinking of the Great Fortune Wheel was caused by its own fault, the ship was insured by the China-America Water and Fire Insurance Company, so there should be no loss in reality. Our company is currently investigating the conclusive evidence and can prove the fault of the Great Fortune Wheel. The evidence will be collected and submitted for approval to the Ministry of Communications for record (excerpt below).

Xu Yabo is Still Detained 136

Yesterday's Confrontation with Li Wenjun

Li Claims Xu is Indeed His Teacher

The Court Must Conduct Further Investigation

Three Women Have Been Released

After Xu Tianxiong, the notorious bandit of Taihu Lake, also known as Taibao Ashu, was captured and executed by Xu Pucheng, the district chief of the First District of the Water Police, his numerous followers dispersed in all directions, making it difficult to prevent them from regrouping and causing disturbances. Therefore, relentless efforts were made to apprehend them. On the morning of the 26th of last month, at 5:00 AM, Chief Xu discovered that Li Wenjun, a subordinate of Taibao Ashu involved in communist activities, and his teacher Xu Yabo (formerly the district chief of the First District of the Water Police) were hiding at No. 96 Annam Road and No. 332 Duofuli, Foch Road, in the Public Concession. He then collaborated with the Jing'an Temple police to arrest Li and Xu, along with Lu Fugen, Qian Moqu, Qian Zhangshi, Qian Xiangrong, Li Weishi, Qian Weirong, Lu Gushi, Wu Qianshi, Jin Linshi, Lu Lishi, Cao Feishi, Chen Asan, and others, and brought them to the Special District Court for a joint interrogation. Except for Chen Wenjun, who was taken back by Chief Xu in court, Qian Moqu, Qian Zhangshi, Qian Xiangrong, and Qian Weirong were released because they were not involved. The remaining individuals were detained separately. This was reported in this newspaper yesterday morning. Judge Ge Zhitan continued the interrogation in the Second Criminal Court. Zhang Tianyin, the police lawyer, stated the case, saying that a witness, Wang Wendao, was present and requested to be questioned. Wang Wendao testified that he lived at No. 332 Duofuli and cohabited with Xu Yabo, also known as Gongshu. Because both he and Xu rented the house from the landlord, the lease was in the name of Wang Gongshu. The Water Police, represented by lawyer Liu Zuwang, requested a transfer and presented various pieces of evidence, claiming that Xu was involved in the robbery of Xu Baiming, a resident near Songjiang Xin Zhuang, on December 12th of last year. Xu Yabo hired three lawyers, Fan Gang, Pan Chenge, and Yuan Xilian, to defend him, arguing that the defendant resided in the concession and should be tried by the court in the defendant's location according to the law. Xu Yabo testified that he previously lived at No. 32 Huanlong Road in the French Concession. Around January of this year, he received a pistol thrown from outside, followed by a threatening letter from Taibao Ashu, which stated that when he was the chief of the First District of the Water Police, many of their followers were arrested and executed. Now that he was still in Shanghai, he should quickly seek death or spend some money to save the souls of the dead. If he agreed to pay, he should write the words "Full Earth Red" on white paper and paste it on the door. After receiving the letter, he thought it was extremely dangerous, so he reported it to the French police. The police ordered him to follow the instructions in the letter to facilitate the arrest, but he did not think it was appropriate and decided to move. He then cohabited with Wang Wendao in Duofuli. Since resigning as the chief of the First District of the Water Police in the 16th year of the Republic, he had been working in the military and political circles. Later, he founded the World Moral Society, but it closed down in the 19th year of the Republic due to a loss of tens of thousands of gold. He had been unemployed ever since. Li Wenjun was also brought to court by Chief Xu. Li testified that Xu Yabo, the defendant in this case, was the Xu Yabo he had previously mentioned. He became Xu's student in December of last year, and Taibao Ashu became Xu's student in January of this year. He and Xu only had a teacher-student relationship, and Xu was not involved in his actions. At this point, the part of the interrogation concerning Xu Yabo ended. The other defendants were then questioned. Chief Xu Pucheng testified that the defendant Lu Fugen was listed in the bandit register, Li Weishi was Lu's wife, originally named Zhang Aiwen, who was in charge of food. Wu Qianshi, also known as Chen Gushi, nicknamed Sister Mei, was the wife of the executed bandit Tang Yixin. Cao Feishi, Ashu's mother, and Chen Asan, Ashu's younger brother, should also be temporarily detained because Ashu had many firearms hidden in wasteland tombs that had not been recovered. The rest of the people were not involved. Judge Ge reviewed the testimonies and ordered Xu Yabo and others to be detained separately for further investigation at a later date. Lu Gushi, Jin Dushi, and Lu Lishi were released.

Detective Liang Chengli is Accused 137

of Robbing a Huge Amount of Morphine 138

Worth More Than 50,000 Yuan

Chinese and Western Detectives Speak with Conviction

Liang Chengyu, from Shandong, has been working as a detective in the Old Gate Police Station for many years. Last year, he was promoted to the head of the Second Chinese Detective Team and transferred to the General Inspection Office of the General Police Station. He resided at No. 756 and a half, Dafangli, South Chengdu Road. At 9:30 AM yesterday morning, Chief Inspector Yok of the Inspection Office, Chief Detective Lu Liankui, and Detective Liu Shaokui suddenly escorted Detective Liang to the Second Criminal Court of the Special District Court, accusing him of conspiring with others on the night of April 28th at 11:00 PM to rob Li Liansheng of morphine worth more than 50,000 yuan at No. 439 Male Li, Chongqing Road, using armed violence and coercion, violating Article 348 of the Criminal Law. The defendant Liang Chengyu hired three lawyers, Ye Fukan, Yuan Yang'an, and Tan Xinzhen. Li Liansheng also hired lawyer Eson to defend him. First, Zhang Tianyin, the police lawyer, presented the case, stating that on the morning of April 28th, at around 7:00 AM, seven robbers, two armed with pistols, broke into a company at No. 1 Wenderli, Jiale Road, and robbed morphine worth 50,000 yuan. They took the stolen goods to the Public Concession, first placing them on Dagu Road, then moving them to Danshui Road, and finally to Li Liansheng's house at No. 439 Old Male Li, Chongqing Road. Li was one of the seven robbers. At around 11:00 PM that night, six robbers, two armed with pistols, broke into Li's house and took all the morphine. The defendant Liang Chengyu was one of the six robbers and distributed the opium between 1:00 AM and 6:00 AM on the 29th, so the stolen goods have not been found. Li reported to the police that he was robbed by Liang and his gang. Inspector Yok ordered Li to identify the robbers and pointed out the defendant from six detectives. The next day, Li's mistress, Zhang Ashi, went to the police station, and the detective ordered six or seven detectives to remove their coats and badges and mix the defendant among them. Zhang first pointed out another detective, No. 110, but then said it was a mistake and pointed out the defendant. However, the defendant denied it at the police station. Chief Inspector Yok also submitted a report to the court explaining the situation, and his testimony was similar to that of lawyer Zhang. Li Liansheng testified that he was a local, 25 years old, and worked in hardware. He lived on the upper floor of the living room at No. 439 Old Male Li, Chongqing Road. On the morning of the 28th of last month, at 7:30 AM, he and Xu Gengen (who was arrested by the French police), Wang Zilian, Mr. Zhang, and others went to Jiale Road and robbed four boxes of morphine worth more than 50,000 yuan. Wang initiated this matter, and Zhang had two pistols. After the incident, Zhang took the pistols and four packages of morphine to the sixth house in Dafangli, Chengdu Road, which was Detective Liang's house. The robbed morphine was first transported to Dagu Road by car. Fearing that the driver would leak the information, it was moved to Danshui Road. Soon after, it was moved to Zhou's house opposite the racecourse. Because Zhou's house was small, it was moved to his house, where he guarded it alone. At 11:00 PM that night, six robbers entered through the back door and went straight to the living room and his bedroom. Detective Liang, Zhu Mapi, and a large man with a sturdy body each held a pistol, forcing him to hand over the keys to open the boxes, shouting that Xu Gengen had been arrested by the French police and demanding that he hand over the goods immediately, promising to give him 30 yuan first and another 3,000 yuan after the goods were sold. Detective Liang was wearing a brown robe and a copper helmet and came with Westerners. He first took away a large leather suitcase containing the morphine. As they were about to move the remaining boxes, they were stopped by the patrol officer at the gate because it was late at night. They changed their plan and took him and his mistress Zhang Ashi to Room 9 of the Jingsheng Inn in Jingshengli behind the Far East Hotel to supervise and discuss. At dawn, around 5:00 AM, they sent two people to watch him and two people accompanied his mistress Zhang Ashi home to open the remaining three boxes, pack them into two shoe baskets, and hire a car to transport them away. Later, he met a detective surnamed Wang, told him what happened, and was taken to the Chief Inspector's office to report and identified the defendant. The woman Zhang Ashi, from Yangzhou, 30 years old, testified that Li Liansheng was her husband and that her testimony was mostly the same as Li's, so it was omitted. The defendant Liang Chengyu testified that he knew nothing about this matter and had taken leave on April 28th and was not working. He did not know Zhu Mapi and the large man. On that day, he went to the French Concession with his friend Dong Lanting and could call Dong to testify. He had arrested Li Liansheng, also known as Fang Liansheng, for his involvement in the kidnapping of Li Huiqing at Gamsdong Road in the French Concession and searched Li's house on Chongqing Road for guns but found nothing. He was now being falsely accused. Finally, lawyer Zhang Tianyin stated to the court that when the defendant was detained, he told Chief Inspector Yok that if he could find the morphine, would he not be taken to court? Yok did not allow this because this statement was concerned with his reputation. Lawyer Zhang then asked the defendant if this had happened, but the defendant denied it. At this point, Judge Ge Zhitan believed that the case required further investigation and additional witnesses, so he ordered the defendant Liang Chengyu to be detained for questioning again on the afternoon of the 15th of this month and allowed Li Liansheng and Zhang Ashi to be detained.

Ye and Chen's Reconciliation is Unlikely 139

Out-of-Court Mediation Failed

Yesterday's Continued Trial, Each Fully Explaining Their Case

The lawsuit between Ye Zhongfang and Chen Xiuzhen was previously heard twice by Judge Xiao Xiefei, who ordered both parties to mediate out of court. As the mediation failed, the hearing was continued yesterday. At 2:30 PM, Judge Xiao opened the third court hearing. Both the plaintiff, defendant, and lawyers were present as scheduled. Ye Zhongfang was no longer wearing a Western suit as before but had changed into a Chinese-style gown. First, Ye's lawyer, Jiang Yiping, stated that the defendant hoped Chen Xiuzhen would return to the Ye family, but the other party was unwilling and only wanted money, so reconciliation was difficult and the court should make a decision. Judge Xiao then questioned the plaintiff, Chen Yan, asking if her daughter could live with Ye Zhongfang again. She replied that they used to live together harmoniously, but now it was impossible. The judge then turned to Chen Xiuzhen and asked if she had lived with Ye for two years and could continue to live with him. Xiuzhen replied that he (referring to Zhongfang) had sent her back to her mother's house last time. Asked when she started living with Ye, she replied December 22nd of the year before last. Asked if her mother knew, she replied no at first. Asked why she had posted a newspaper notice, she replied that Ye had asked lawyer Zhang Ding to do it. Asked if it was her intention, she replied that he had thought of it for her. Asked if the notice included the phrase "separate from her mother and have marital autonomy," she replied that he had taught her to say that. She was only seventeen the year before last, and if she did not agree, he would force her to smoke opium and often threaten her with sulfuric acid and pistols. She was afraid of him, so she followed his instructions to post the notice. Asked why she was afraid of him, she replied that she had to go to the dance hall at night and return home late, fearing harm. Asked how long Ye lived in her house, she replied that their spare room was rented to him, but he did not come to stay at night. Asked why he rented it if he did not stay, she replied that she did not know. Asked if she had told her mother when she left with Ye on December 22nd the year before last, she replied that she had not. Asked what Ye said they were going to do, she replied eat snacks. Asked where her mother was, she replied that they were supposed to meet at the train station. Asked why she did not go to the train station, she replied that he did not allow her to return. Asked if she was willing to follow Ye, she replied that he wanted her, but she was afraid of him. Asked why she was not afraid of her mother, she replied that her mother did not have sulfuric acid and pistols. Asked how long she lived in Ye's house, she replied about five or six months. Asked if her mother had looked for her, she replied that she knew she had been taken away by Ye, so she did not look for her. Asked if she knew that her mother had reported it to the police, she replied that she did not know. The judge then questioned the defendant, Ye Zhongfang, asking what he had to say in response to the plaintiff's accusation that he had abducted her daughter. Ye replied that he had said everything last time. In short, her mother had ordered her daughter to accompany him because he was drunk that day and could not return home, so her mother allowed him to stay overnight and ordered her daughter to sleep with him. This kind of behavior should not be considered seduction. Asked if he had any evidence to refute the plaintiff's accusation of abduction, he replied that he had gone to buy furniture with the daughter when he rented the room, so it was not abduction. Asked if he knew that the daughter was not of age and had no autonomy, he replied that she had taught him everything. Asked if it was true that the mother had allowed it, but now she objected, he replied that if she said he had abducted her, why had she not accused him earlier? They had mediated with each other between August and September of last year, and he had agreed to pay 1,500 yuan to resolve the matter, but he did not have the money at the time, which led to today's situation. Asked about the newspaper notice, Chen Xiuzhen testified that it was Ye's idea. He replied that anyone who had lost their conscience could say anything, but the lawyer representing the publication of the notice was well-versed in the law and would not have been so rash. At this point, the plaintiff's lawyer, Xue Jiaqi, stated that the court believed that the mother's testimony that she had reported the case to the police required further investigation, so he stated that the mother had reported it to the Loujiawan Police Station in the French Concession, which could be investigated to clarify the matter. The judge then asked Chen Yan about the rental situation. She replied that Ye had rented the living room upstairs in their house for 22 yuan a month. Ye's friends were all men, and she did not go to his room, but Ye did not live in that room at night. She did not know about her daughter's relationship with him at first. This year, because he beat her daughter, the mother sent her daughter back home. Lawyer Jiang then cross-examined the mother, but she was unwilling to answer many questions or gave irrelevant answers. Lawyer Jiang then proposed questions for the judge to ask. The judge announced that the case would be postponed and continued on the 20th of this month. Both parties then left.

Spring Cold Affects Silkworm Rearing 142

Hatching is Delayed and Development is Poor

According to an investigation by local silk merchants, this spring, due to the cold weather around Qingming, silkworm farmers have been greatly affected. Recently, farmers in Hangyu and Linping have reported that their silkworms died from the cold twice, before and after hatching. The last ones that were raised were also difficult to thrive because they hatched later. Moreover, Chinese farmers do not know how to improve their breeding grounds and feeding methods, and the quality of silk is deteriorating day by day. It is predicted that this year's silkworm cocoon harvest will be difficult to be abundant.

Sandboat Sinks in Hurricane 143

Seven Crew Members Missing

One Person Drifts to Safety

The northern sandboat Chen Wantai loaded a large amount of soybean cakes and groceries from Taihuangdao and sailed to Shanghai. On the afternoon of the 5th (yesterday), at about 4:00 PM, it sailed to the Tongsha waters outside the harbor. A hurricane broke out, and the captain was careless and ran aground on a reef, causing the bottom of the boat to crack and sink immediately. There were eight crew members on board, all of whom fell into the water. Seven of them are missing. One crew member named Zou Sixi was lucky enough to grab a plank when the boat sank. He drifted with the waves all night and drifted to the Sanjia Shui waters at about 8:00 AM yesterday morning. He was spotted by an ice-fresh fishing boat, rescued, and taken to Wusong. The crew member arrived in Shanghai and took a car to report to the company.
